[\xe2\x80\xa6] War with Iraq may yet not come, but, conscious of the potentially terrifying responsibility resting with the British Government, we find ourselves supporting the current commitment to a possible use of force."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> But <i>The Guardian</i> opposed the war, along with the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror"><i>Daily Mirror</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Then <i>Guardian</i> features editor Ian Katz asserted in 2004 that "it is no secret we are a centre-left newspaper".<sup id="cite_ref-undecidedvoters_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undecidedvoters-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, <i>Guardian</i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Ashley" title="Jackie Ashley">Jackie Ashley</a> said that editorial contributors were a mix of "right-of-centre <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarians</a>, greens, Blairites, Brownites, Labourite but less enthusiastic Brownites, etc," and that the newspaper was "clearly left of centre and vaguely progressive". She also said that "you can be absolutely certain that come the next general election, <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> stance will not be dictated by the editor, still less any foreign proprietor (it helps that there isn\'t one) but will be the result of vigorous debate within the paper".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardianistas_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardianistas-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The paper\'s comment and opinion pages, though often written by centre-left contributors such as <a href="/wiki/Polly_Toynbee" title="Polly Toynbee">Polly Toynbee</a>, have allowed some space for right-of-centre voices such as <a href="/wiki/Max_Hastings" title="Max Hastings">Sir Max Hastings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gove" title="Michael Gove">Michael Gove</a>. Since an editorial in 2000, <i>The Guardian</i> has favoured abolition of the British monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> "I write for the <i>Guardian</i>," said Max Hastings in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> "because it is read by the new establishment," reflecting the paper\'s then-growing influence.\n</p><p>In the run-up to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>, following a meeting of the editorial staff,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> the paper declared its support for the Liberal Democrats, due in particular, to the party\'s stance on <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform" title="Electoral reform">electoral reform</a>. The paper suggested <a href="/wiki/Tactical_voting" title="Tactical voting">tactical voting</a> to prevent a Conservative victory, given Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a> electoral system.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">the 2015 election</a>, the paper switched its support to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. The paper argued that Britain needed a new direction and Labour "speaks with more urgency than its rivals on social justice, standing up to predatory capitalism, on investment for growth, on reforming and strengthening the public realm, Britain\'s place in Europe and international development".<sup id="cite_ref-lab2015_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lab2015-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Assistant Editor Michael White, in discussing media self-censorship in March 2011, says: "I have always sensed liberal, middle class ill-ease in going after stories about immigration, legal or otherwise, about welfare fraud or the less attractive tribal habits of the working class, which is more easily ignored altogether. Toffs, including royal ones, Christians, especially popes, governments of Israel, and US <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> are more straightforward targets."<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a 2013 interview for <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>, the <i>Guardian\'s</i> Latin America correspondent <a href="/wiki/Rory_Carroll" title="Rory Carroll">Rory Carroll</a> stated that many editors at <i>The Guardian</i> believed and continue to believe that they should support <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez</a> "because he was a standard-bearer for the left".<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2013_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2013-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)_leadership_election,_2015" title="Labour Party (UK) leadership election, 2015">2015 Labour Party leadership election</a>, <i>The Guardian</i> supported <a href="/wiki/Yvette_Cooper" title="Yvette Cooper">Yvette Cooper</a> and was critical of left-winger <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, the successful candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> These positions were criticised by the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Morning_star" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="The Morning star">Morning Star</a></i>, which accused <i>The Guardian</i> of being conservative.<sup id="cite_ref-MS1_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MS1-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Although the majority of political columnists in <i>The Guardian</i> were against Corbyn winning, <a href="/wiki/Owen_Jones_(writer)" title="Owen Jones (writer)">Owen Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seumas_Milne" title="Seumas Milne">Seumas Milne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Monbiot" title="George Monbiot">George Monbiot</a> wrote supportive articles about him. \n</p><p>Despite this critical position, in the 2017 election <i>The Guardian</i> endorsed the Labour Party.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Journalist <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Greenwald" title="Glenn Greenwald">Glenn Greenwald</a> of <i>The Intercept</i>, a former contributor to <i>The Guardian</i>, has accused <i>The Guardian</i> of falsifying the words of <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Julian_Assange" title="Julian Assange">Julian Assange</a> in a report about the interview he gave to Italian newspaper <i>La Repubblica.</i> Greenwald wrote: "This article is about how those [<i>Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span>] false claims \xe2\x80\x94 fabrications, really \xe2\x80\x94 were spread all over the internet by journalists, causing hundreds of thousands of people (if not millions) to consume false news."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> later retracted its article about Assange.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After publishing a story on 13 January 2017 claiming that <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp</a> had a "backdoor [that] allows snooping on messages", more than 70 professional cryptographers signed on to an open letter calling for <i>The Guardian</i> to retract the article. Security researchers also criticised the story, including <a href="/wiki/Moxie_Marlinspike" title="Moxie Marlinspike">Moxie Marlinspike</a> who called it "false".<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On 13 June 2017, editor Paul Chadwick released an article detailing the flawed reporting in the original January article, which was amended to remove references to a backdoor.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Circulation_and_format">Circulation and format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Circulation and format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> had a certified average daily circulation of 204,222 copies in December 2012&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 a drop of 11.25 per cent on January 2012&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 as compared to sales of 547,465 for <i>The Daily Telegraph</i>, 396,041 for <i>The Times</i>, and 78,082 for <i>The Independent</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, its average daily circulation had fallen to 193,586, according to the Audit Bureau of Circulations.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Circulation has continued to decline and stood at 161,091 in December 2016, a decline of 2.98 per cent year-on-year.<sup id="cite_ref-circ_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circ-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publication_history">Publication history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Publication history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GuardianNewsroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/220px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/330px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/GuardianNewsroom.jpg/440px-GuardianNewsroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GuardianNewsroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Newsroom visitor centre and archive (No 60), with an old sign with the name <i>The Manchester Guardian</i></div></div></div>\n<p>The first edition was published on 5 May 1821,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> at which time <i>The Guardian</i> was a weekly, published on Saturdays and costing 7<a href="/wiki/Penny" title="Penny">d</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_duty" title="Stamp duty">stamp duty</a> on newspapers (4d per sheet) forced the price up so high that it was uneconomic to publish more frequently. When the stamp duty was cut in 1836, <i>The Guardian</i> added a Wednesday edition and with the abolition of the tax in 1855 it became a daily paper costing 2d.\n</p><p>In October 1952, the paper took the step of printing news on the front page, replacing the adverts that had hitherto filled that space. Then-editor A. P. Wadsworth wrote: "It is not a thing I like myself, but it seems to be accepted by all the newspaper pundits that it is preferable to be in fashion."<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1959, the paper dropped "Manchester" from its title, becoming simply <i>The Guardian</i>, and in 1964 it moved to London, losing some of its regional agenda but continuing to be heavily subsidised by sales of the more downmarket but more profitable <i>Manchester Evening News</i>. The financial position remained extremely poor into the 1970s; at one time it was in merger talks with <i>The Times</i>. The paper consolidated its centre-left stance during the 1970s and 1980s. It was both shocked and revitalised by the launch of <i>The Independent</i> in 1986 which competed for a similar readership and provoked the entire broadsheet industry into a fight for circulation.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg/220px-Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/ba/Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="269" data-file-height="369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sima_Wali_on_the_front_page_of_The_Guardian_newspaper_in_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front page of <i>The Guardian</i> from 2001, showing the old design of the paper when in broadsheet format. This design was used from 1988 to 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>On 12 February 1988, <i>The Guardian</i> had a significant redesign; as well as improving the quality of its printers\' ink, it also changed its masthead to a juxtaposition of an <a href="/wiki/Italic_type" title="Italic type">italic</a> <a href="/wiki/Garamond" title="Garamond">Garamond</a> "<i>The</i>", with a bold <a href="/wiki/Helvetica" title="Helvetica">Helvetica</a> "Guardian", that remained in use until the 2005 redesign.\n</p><p>In 1992, <i>The Guardian</i> relaunched its features section as <i>G2</i>, a tabloid-format supplement. This innovation was widely copied by the other "quality" broadsheets and ultimately led to the rise of "compact" papers and <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> move to the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_(format)" title="Berliner (format)">Berliner format</a>. In 1993 the paper declined to participate in the broadsheet <a href="/wiki/Price_war" title="Price war">price war</a> started by <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a>\'s <i>The Times</i>. In June 1993, <i>The Guardian</i> bought <i>The Observer</i> from <a href="/wiki/Lonrho" title="Lonrho">Lonrho</a>, thus gaining a serious <a href="/wiki/Sunday_editions" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday editions">Sunday sister newspaper</a> with similar political views.\n</p><p>Its international weekly edition is now titled <i>The Guardian Weekly</i>, though it retained the title <i>Manchester Guardian Weekly</i> for some years after the home edition had moved to London. It includes sections from a number of other internationally significant newspapers of a somewhat left-of-centre inclination, including <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>. <i>The Guardian Weekly</i> was also linked to a website for expatriates, <i>Guardian Abroad</i>, which was launched in 2007 but had been taken offline by 2012.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moving_to_the_Berliner_paper_format">Moving to the Berliner paper format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Moving to the Berliner paper format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg/220px-The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="387" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Guardian_6._6._14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front page of the 6th June 2014 edition in the Berliner format.</div></div></div>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> is printed in full colour,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and was the first newspaper in the UK to use the Berliner format for its main section, while producing sections and supplements in a range of page sizes including tabloid, approximately A4, and pocket-size (approximately A5).\n</p><p>In 2004, <i>The Guardian</i> announced plans to change to a Berliner or "<a href="/wiki/Midi_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Midi (newspaper)">midi</a>" format, similar to that used by <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Tageszeitung" title="Die Tageszeitung">Die Tageszeitung</a></i> in Germany, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> in France and many other European papers. At 470\xc3\x97315&#160;mm, this is slightly larger than a traditional <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid</a>. Planned for the autumn of 2005, this change followed moves by <i>The Independent</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> to start publishing in tabloid (or compact) format. On Thursday, 1 September 2005, <i>The Guardian</i> announced that it would launch the new format on Monday 12 September 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Sister Sunday newspaper <i>The Observer</i> also changed to this new format on 8 January 2006.\n</p><p>The advantage <i>The Guardian</i> saw in the Berliner format was that, though it is only a little wider than a tabloid, and is equally easy to read on public transport, its greater height gives more flexibility in page design. The new presses mean that printing can go across the strip down the middle of the centre page, known as the "gutter", allowing the paper to print striking double-page pictures. The new presses also made it the first UK national paper to print in full colour on every page.\n</p><p>The format switch was accompanied by a comprehensive redesign of the paper\'s look. On Friday, 9 September 2005, the newspaper unveiled its newly designed front page, which d\xc3\xa9buted on Monday 12 September 2005. Designed by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Porter_(designer)" title="Mark Porter (designer)">Mark Porter</a>, the new look includes a new <a href="/wiki/Masthead_(publishing)" title="Masthead (publishing)">masthead</a> for the newspaper, its first since 1988. A typeface family designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barnes_(designer)" title="Paul Barnes (designer)">Paul Barnes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Schwartz" title="Christian Schwartz">Christian Schwartz</a> was created for the new design. With just over 200 fonts, it is "one of the most ambitious custom type programs ever commissioned by a newspaper".<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fontshop2006_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fontshop2006-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Especially notable is <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Egyptian" title="Guardian Egyptian">Guardian Egyptian</a>, a highly legible <a href="/wiki/Slab_serif" title="Slab serif">slab serif</a> that is used in various weights for both text and headlines and is central to the redesign.\n</p><p>The switch cost <i>Guardian Newspapers</i> \xc2\xa380&#160;million and involved setting up new printing presses in east London and Manchester. This switch was necessary because, before <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> move, no printing presses in Britain could produce newspapers in the Berliner format. There were additional complications, as one of the paper\'s presses was part-owned by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">Telegraph Newspapers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="The Daily Express">Express Newspapers</a></i>, contracted to use the plant until 2009. Another press was shared with the <i>Guardian Media Group\'s</i> north-western tabloid local papers, which did not wish to switch to the Berliner format.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The new format was generally well received by <i>Guardian</i> readers, who were encouraged to provide feedback on the changes. The only controversy was over the dropping of the <i><a href="/wiki/Doonesbury" title="Doonesbury">Doonesbury</a></i> cartoon strip. The paper reported thousands of calls and emails complaining about its loss; within 24 hours the decision was reversed and the strip was reinstated the following week. <i>G2</i> supplement editor Ian Katz, who was responsible for dropping it, apologised in the editors\' blog saying, "I\'m sorry, once again, that I made you\xe2\x80\x94and the hundreds of fellow fans who have called our helpline or mailed our comments\' address\xe2\x80\x94so cross."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> However, some readers were dissatisfied as the earlier deadline needed for the all-colour sports section meant coverage of late-finishing evening football matches became less satisfactory in the editions supplied to some parts of the country.\n</p><p>The investment was rewarded with a circulation rise. In December 2005, the average daily sale stood at 380,693, nearly 6 per cent higher than the figure for December 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> (However, as of December 2012, circulation had dropped to 204,222.)<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the US-based <a href="/wiki/Society_for_News_Design" title="Society for News Design">Society for News Design</a> chose <i>The Guardian</i> and Polish daily <i><a href="/wiki/Rzeczpospolita_(newspaper)" title="Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)">Rzeczpospolita</a></i> as the world\'s best-designed newspapers\xe2\x80\x94from among 389 entries from 44 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tabloid_format_since_2018">Tabloid format since 2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tabloid format since 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In June 2017, <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Media_Group" title="Guardian Media Group">Guardian Media Group</a> (GMG) announced that <i>The Guardian</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> will relaunch in <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid format</a> from early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-tabloid_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tabloid-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> confirmed that the launch date for the new format will be 15 January 2018. The first tabloid format <i>Observer</i> will therefore appear on 21 January. GMG also signed a contract with <i><a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 the publisher of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mirror" title="Sunday Mirror">Sunday Mirror</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday People">Sunday People</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 to <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">outsource</a> printing of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The format change is intended to help cut cost as it allows the paper to be printed by a wider array of presses, and outsourcing the printing to presses owned by Trinity Mirror is expected to generate millions of pounds in savings annually.  The move is part of a three-year plan that includes cutting 300 jobs in an attempt to reduce losses to break even point by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-tabloid_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tabloid-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The paper and ink are the same as previously and the font size is fractionally larger.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An assessment of the response from readers in late April 2018 indicated that the new format had led to an increased number of subscriptions. The editors were working on changing aspects that had caused complaints from readers.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_content_and_features">Regular content and features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Regular content and features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>With the main paper now a tabloid as of 2018, all week-day supplements are of the same size as the main section.  Opinion and idea features are in a second section called <i>Journal</i>, while G2 contains lighter items and features.  Saturday\'s edition contains a glossy magazine called <i>Weekend</i> and a smaller stapled listings and culture supplement called <i>The Guide</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Every_weekday_content">Every weekday content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Every weekday content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dt>In <i>Journal</i></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Leader column</li>\n<li>Editorial cartoon by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Rowson" title="Martin Rowson">Martin Rowson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bell_(cartoonist)" title="Steve Bell (cartoonist)">Steve Bell</a>, Ben Jennings, Nicola Jennings, <a href="/wiki/First_Dog_on_the_Moon" class="mw-redirect" title="First Dog on the Moon">First Dog on the Moon</a> and others.</li>\n<li>Obituaries</li>\n<li>Puzzles</li>\n<li>Letters</li>\n<li>Corrections and Clarifications</li>\n<li>Country Diary</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>In <i>G2</i></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Pass Notes</li>\n<li>Shortcuts</li>\n<li>Arts</li>\n<li>TV and Radio</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/If..._(comic)" title="If... (comic)">If...</a></i> (comic strip by Steve Bell)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day-specific_content">Day-specific content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Day-specific content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<dl><dt>Monday</dt></dl>\n<p>In the main paper:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Media</li></ul>\n<p>In <i>G2</i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Rhik Samadder\'s column</li>\n<li><i>Private Lives</i> (<a href="/wiki/Advice_column" title="Advice column">advice column</a> on personal problems answered by other readers)</li>\n<li><i>Sexual Healing</i> (Sex advice column by <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Stephenson_Connolly" class="mw-redirect" title="Pamela Stephenson Connolly">Pamela Stephenson Connolly</a>)</li>\n<li><i> The Digested Read</i> (humorous book summary by <a href="/wiki/John_Crace_(writer)" title="John Crace (writer)">John Crace</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Tuesday</dt></dl>\n<p>In the main paper:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Education</li></ul>\n<p>In <i>G2</i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Moore" title="Suzanne Moore">Suzanne Moore</a>\'s column</li>\n<li><i>How We Made</i>, feature about the birth of a work or object</li>\n<li><i>Wide Awoke</i> (Chitra Ramaswany\'s column)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Notes_%26_Queries" title="Notes &amp; Queries">Notes &amp; Queries</a></i> (readers ask and answer each other questions on any topic)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Wednesday</dt></dl>\n<p>In the main paper:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Society (covers the British <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> and related issues)\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Clare_in_the_Community" title="Clare in the Community">Clare in the Community</a></i> (comic strip by Harry Venning)</li></ul></li></ul>\n<p>In <i>G2</i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Arwa Mahdawi\'s column</li>\n<li><i>Working It Out</i>, (advice column on work problems answered by other readers)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Thursday</dt></dl>\n<p>In <i>G2</i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Zoe_Williams" title="Zoe Williams">Zoe Williams</a> column</li>\n<li>Food\n<ul><li><i>Fast Food</i> recipe</li>\n<li><i>The Faddy Eater</i> by Morwenna Ferrier</li></ul></li>\n<li><i>Ask Hadley</i>: <a href="/wiki/Hadley_Freeman" title="Hadley Freeman">Hadley Freeman</a> answers reader queries theoretically about style and fashion</li>\n<li><i>My Best Shot</i> (photography feature)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Friday</dt></dl>\n<p>In <i>G2</i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Lost in Showbiz</i> (corrosive column by <a href="/wiki/Marina_Hyde" title="Marina Hyde">Marina Hyde</a> and others)</li>\n<li>Film &amp; Music</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Doonesbury" title="Doonesbury">Doonesbury</a></i> (now weekly comic strip by <a href="/wiki/Garry_Trudeau" title="Garry Trudeau">Garry Trudeau</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Saturday</dt></dl>\n<p><i>The Guide</i> (a weekly <a href="/wiki/Listings_magazine" title="Listings magazine">listings magazine</a>)\n</p>\n<ul><li>Infomania (humorous statistical data on a topical personality or institution)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Toss" title="Modern Toss">Home-Clubber</a></i> (cartoon)</li></ul>\n<p><i>Weekend</i> (supplement)\n</p>\n<ul><li>Starters\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hadley_Freeman" title="Hadley Freeman">Hadley Freeman</a> weekend column</li>\n<li><i>Briefly Noted</i>, (Bim Adewunmi\'s column)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tim_Dowling" title="Tim Dowling">Tim Dowling</a> (eponymous diary column)</li>\n<li>Q&amp;A interview</li>\n<li><i>Experience</i> (Interview with a person about an unusual experience)</li></ul></li>\n<li>Fashion\n<ul><li>Blind Date</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jess_Cartner-Morley" title="Jess Cartner-Morley">Jess Cartner-Morley</a> on fashion</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sali_Hughes" title="Sali Hughes">Sali Hughes</a>\'s beauty column</li></ul></li>\n<li>Space\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Alys_Fowler" title="Alys Fowler">Alys Fowler</a> gardening column</li>\n<li><i>Let\'s move to</i> (relocation feature)</li></ul></li>\n<li>Family\n<ul><li><i>Ask Annalisa Barbieri</i> (family <a href="/wiki/Advice_column" title="Advice column">advice column</a>)</li>\n<li>The Secret to...</li></ul></li>\n<li>Body &amp; Mind\n<ul><li>Oliver Burkeman column</li>\n<li><i>The Balance</i></li>\n<li><i>Bossing it</i></li>\n<li><i>My Life in Sex</i>, by a different anonymous reader</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zoe_Williams" title="Zoe Williams">Zoe Williams</a> column</li></ul></li>\n<li>Back\n<ul><li>Coco Khan\'s column</li></ul></li></ul>\n<p><i>Review</i> (covers literature, cinema and arts)\n</p><p><i>Travel</i>\n</p><p><i>Feast</i> (food supplement)\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yotam_Ottolenghi" title="Yotam Ottolenghi">Yotam Ottolenghi</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomasina_Miers" title="Thomasina Miers">Thomasina Miers</a></li>\n<li>Anna Jones</li>\n<li>Fiona Beckett (wine column)</li>\n<li>Meera Sodha</li>\n<li>Tamal Ray</li>\n<li>Felicity Cloake</li>\n<li>Rachel Roddy</li>\n<li><i>Can I cook like...</i> by Stephen Bush</li>\n<li>Rosie Birkett</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grace_Dent" title="Grace Dent">Grace Dent</a>\'s restaurant review</li></ul></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_media">Online media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Online media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/TheGuardian.com" title="TheGuardian.com">TheGuardian.com</a></div>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> and its Sunday sibling <i>The Observer</i> publish all their news online, with free access both to current news and an archive of three million stories. A third of the site\'s hits are for items over a month old.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> As of May 2013, it was the most popular UK newspaper website with 8.2 million unique visitors per month, just ahead of <i><a href="/wiki/Mail_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="Mail Online">Mail Online</a></i> with 7.6 million unique monthly visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism553108_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism553108-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In April 2011, <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Media_Group" title="Haymarket Media Group">MediaWeek</a> reported that <i>The Guardian</i> was the fifth most popular newspaper site in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Comment_is_Free" class="mw-redirect" title="Comment is Free">Comment is Free</a> section features columns by the paper\'s journalists and regular commentators, as well as articles from guest writers, including readers\' comments and responses below. The section includes all the opinion pieces published in the paper itself, as well as many others that only appear online. Censorship is exercised by Moderators who can ban posts&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 with no right of appeal&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 by those who they feel have overstepped the mark. <i>The Guardian</i> has taken what they call a very "open" stance in delivering news, and have launched an open platform for their content. This allows external developers to easily use <i>Guardian</i> content in external applications, and even to feed third-party content back into the <i>Guardian</i> network.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> also had a number of talkboards that were noted for their mix of political discussion and whimsy until they were closed on Friday, 25 February 2011 after they had settled a libel action brought after months of harassment of a conservative party activist.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> They were spoofed in <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> own regular humorous Chatroom column in <i>G2</i>. The spoof column purported to be excerpts from a chatroom on permachat.co.uk, a real URL that pointed to <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> talkboards.\n</p><p>In August 2013, a webshow titled <i>Thinkfluencer</i><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> was launched by <i>Guardian Multimedia</i> in association with <i><a href="/wiki/Arte" title="Arte">Arte</a></i>.\n</p><p>The paper has also launched a dating website, Soulmates,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> and is experimenting with new media, having previously offered a free twelve part weekly <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> series by <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Gervais\' show topped the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> podcast chart having been downloaded by two million listeners worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and was scheduled to be listed in the 2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of Records">Guinness Book of Records</a></i> as the most downloaded podcast.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GuardianFilms">GuardianFilms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: GuardianFilms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2003, <i>The Guardian</i> started the film production company GuardianFilms, headed by journalist Maggie O\'Kane. Much of the company\'s output is documentary made for television\xe2\x80\x93 and it has included <a href="/wiki/Salam_Pax" title="Salam Pax">Salam Pax</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Blogger" class="mw-redirect" title="Baghdad Blogger">Baghdad Blogger</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a>\'s daily flagship <i><a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">Newsnight</a></i>, some of which have been shown in compilations by <i><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> International</i>, <i>Sex On The Streets</i> and <i>Spiked</i>, both made for the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> television.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>"GuardianFilms was born in a sleeping bag in the Burmese <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a>," wrote O\'Kane in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> "I was a foreign correspondent for the paper, and it had taken me weeks of negotiations, dealing with shady contacts and a lot of walking to reach the cigar-smoking Karen twins\xe2\x80\x93 the boy soldiers who were leading attacks against the country\'s ruling junta. After I had reached them and written a cover story for the newspaper\'s <i>G2</i> section, I got a call from the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s documentary department, which was researching a film on child soldiers. Could I give them all my contacts?\n</p><p>"The plight of the Karen people, who were forced into slave labour in the rainforest to build pipelines for oil companies (some of them British), was a tale of human suffering that needed to be told by any branch of the media that was interested. I handed over all the names and numbers I had, as well as details of the secret route through <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> to get into <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a>. Good girl. Afterwards\xe2\x80\x93 and not for the first time\xe2\x80\x93 it seemed to me that we at <i>The Guardian</i> should be using our resources ourselves. Instead of providing contact numbers for any independent TV company prepared to get on the phone to a journalist, we should make our own films."\n</p><p>According to GuardianFilms\'s own webpage, its international work has focused on training talented local journalists based on the premise that "the era of a traditional London or Washington based foreign correspondent or fireman is coming to an end and the world urgently needs a more searching, challenging journalism brought to us by people who speak the language and can secure access far beyond the \'Green Zone Journalist\' limits of the traditional correspondent". It says it is especially focused on reporting the Muslim world in a more challenging manner, and has trained a number of journalists in Iraq, Afghanistan and Zimbabwe.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>GuardianFilms has received several broadcasting awards. In addition to two Amnesty International Media Awards in 2004 and 2005, <i>The Baghdad Blogger: Salam Pax</i> won a Royal Television Society Award in 2005. <i>Baghdad: A Doctor\'s Story</i> won an Emmy Award for Best International Current Affairs film in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Smith_(photojournalist_and_filmmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Smith (photojournalist and filmmaker)">photojournalist Sean Smith\'s</a> <i>Inside the Surge</i> won the Royal Television Society award for best international news film&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the first time a newspaper has won such an award.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The same year, <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Katine" title="Katine">Katine</a> website was awarded for its outstanding new media output at the One World Media awards. Again in 2008, GuardianFilms\' undercover video report revealing vote rigging by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Zanu_PF" class="mw-redirect" title="Zanu PF">Zanu PF</a> party during the 2007 Zimbabwe election won best news programme of the year at the Broadcast Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_in_popular_culture">References in popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: References in popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The paper\'s nickname <i>The Grauniad</i> (sometimes abbreviated as "Graun") originated with the satirical magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Private_Eye_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Private Eye (magazine)">Private Eye</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Anagram" title="Anagram">anagram</a> played on <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s early reputation for frequent <a href="/wiki/Typographical_error" title="Typographical error">typographical errors</a>, including misspelling its own name as <i>The Gaurdian</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The very first issue of the newspaper contained a number of errors, including a notification that there would soon be some goods sold at <i>atction</i> instead of <i>auction</i>. Fewer typographical errors are seen in the paper since the end of <a href="/wiki/Hot_metal_typesetting" title="Hot metal typesetting">hot-metal typesetting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> One <i>Guardian</i> writer, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Devlin" title="Keith Devlin">Keith Devlin</a>, suggested that the high number of observed misprints was due more to the quality of the readership than the misprints\' greater frequency.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The fact that the newspaper was printed in Manchester until 1961 and the early, more error-prone, prints were sent to London by train may have contributed to this image as well.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/John_Cole_(journalist)" title="John Cole (journalist)">John Cole</a> was appointed news editor by <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Hetherington" title="Alastair Hetherington">Alastair Hetherington</a> in 1963, he sharpened the paper\'s comparatively "amateurish" setup.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_obit_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_obit-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Received">Received</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Received">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(June 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> has been awarded the National Newspaper of the Year in 1998, 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> and 2013<sup id="cite_ref-award_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/British_Press_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="British Press Awards">British Press Awards</a>, and Front Page of the Year in 2002 ("A declaration of war", 12 September 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> It was also co-winner of the World\'s Best-designed Newspaper as awarded by the Society for News Design (2006).\n</p><p><i>Guardian</i> journalists have won a range of British Press Awards, including:<sup id="cite_ref-gazetteroll_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazetteroll-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Reporter of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Nick_Davies" title="Nick Davies">Nick Davies</a>, 1999; <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lewis_(journalist)" title="Paul Lewis (journalist)">Paul Lewis</a>, 2009; Rob Evans &amp; Paul Lewis, 2013);</li>\n<li>Foreign Reporter of the Year (<a href="/wiki/James_Meek_(author)" title="James Meek (author)">James Meek</a>, 2003; <a href="/wiki/Ghaith_Abdul-Ahad" title="Ghaith Abdul-Ahad">Ghaith Abdul-Ahad</a>, 2007);</li>\n<li>Scoop of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Milly_Dowler" class="mw-redirect" title="Milly Dowler">Milly Dowler</a> phone hacked, 2011)</li>\n<li>Young Journalist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Emma_Brockes" title="Emma Brockes">Emma Brockes</a>, 2000; Patrick Kingsley, 2013);</li>\n<li>Columnist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Polly_Toynbee" title="Polly Toynbee">Polly Toynbee</a>, 2006; <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Brooker" title="Charlie Brooker">Charlie Brooker</a>, 2008);</li>\n<li>Critic of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Marina_O%27Loughlin" title="Marina O&#39;Loughlin">Marina O\'Loughlin</a>, 2015);</li>\n<li>Feature Writer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Emma_Brockes" title="Emma Brockes">Emma Brockes</a>, 2001; <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Gold" title="Tanya Gold">Tanya Gold</a>, 2009; <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Gentleman" title="Amelia Gentleman">Amelia Gentleman</a>, 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Cartoonist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Bell_(cartoonist)" title="Steve Bell (cartoonist)">Steve Bell</a>, 2002);</li>\n<li>Political Journalist of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Patrick_Wintour" title="Patrick Wintour">Patrick Wintour</a>, 2006; Andrew Sparrow, 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian06042011_194-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian06042011-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Science &amp; Health Journalist of the Year (Sarah Boseley, 2015);</li>\n<li>Business &amp; Finance Journalist of the Year (Ian Griffiths, 2004; Simon Goodley, 2014);</li>\n<li>Interviewer of the Year (<a href="/wiki/Decca_Aitkenhead" title="Decca Aitkenhead">Decca Aitkenhead</a>, 2008);</li>\n<li>Sports Reporter of the Year (David Lacey, 2002);</li>\n<li>Sports Photographer of the Year (Tom Jenkins, 2003, 2005, 2006, 2015);</li>\n<li>Website of the Year (guardian.com/uk, 1999, 2001, 2007, 2008, 2015);</li>\n<li>Digital Journalist of the Year (Dan Milmo, 2001; Sean Smith, 2007; Dave Hill, 2008)</li>\n<li>Supplement of the Year (<i>Guardian\'s Guides to...</i>, 2006; <i>Weekend Magazine</i>, 2015)</li>\n<li>Special Supplement of the Year (<i>World Cup 2010 Guide</i>, 2010)</li></ul>\n<p>Other awards include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bevins_Prize" title="Bevins Prize">Bevins Prize</a> for investigative journalism (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Lewis_(journalist)" title="Paul Lewis (journalist)">Paul Lewis</a>, 2010);</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Martha_Gellhorn_Prize_for_Journalism" title="Martha Gellhorn Prize for Journalism">Martha Gellhorn Prize for Journalism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nick_Davies" title="Nick Davies">Nick Davies</a>, 1999; <a href="/wiki/Chris_McGreal" title="Chris McGreal">Chris McGreal</a>, 2003; <a href="/wiki/Ghaith_Abdul-Ahad" title="Ghaith Abdul-Ahad">Ghaith Abdul-Ahad</a>, 2005; <a href="/wiki/Ian_Cobain" title="Ian Cobain">Ian Cobain</a>, 2009).</li></ul>\n<p>The <i>guardian.co.uk</i> website won the Best Newspaper category three years running in 2005, 2006 and 2007 <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" title="Webby Award">Webby Awards</a>, beating (in 2005) <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, <i>The Washington Post</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> It has been the winner for six years in a row of the British Press Awards for Best Electronic Daily Newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The site won an <i><a href="/wiki/Editor_%26_Publisher" title="Editor &amp; Publisher">Eppy</a></i> award from the US-based magazine <i>Editor &amp; Publisher</i> in 2000 for the best-designed newspaper online service.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The website is known for its commentary on sporting events, particularly its over-by-over cricket commentary.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, the newspaper was ranked first in a study on transparency that analysed 25 mainstream English-language media vehicles, which was conducted by the International Center for Media and the Public Agenda of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> It scored 3.8 out of a possible 4.0.\n</p><p><i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Washington Post</i> shared the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Public_Service" title="Pulitzer Prize for Public Service">Pulitzer Prize for public service reporting</a> for their coverage of the NSA\'s and GCHQ\'s worldwide electronic surveillance program and the document leaks by whistleblower Edward Snowden.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Given">Given</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Given">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> is the sponsor of two major literary awards: The <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_First_Book_Award" title="Guardian First Book Award">Guardian First Book Award</a></i>, established in 1999 as a successor to the <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Fiction_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardian Fiction Award">Guardian Fiction Award</a></i>, which had run since 1965, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Children%27s_Fiction_Prize" title="Guardian Children&#39;s Fiction Prize">Guardian Children\'s Fiction Prize</a></i>, founded in 1967. In recent years the newspaper has also sponsored the <a href="/wiki/Hay_Festival" title="Hay Festival">Hay Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hay-on-Wye" title="Hay-on-Wye">Hay-on-Wye</a>.\n</p><p>The annual <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Student_Media_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardian Student Media Awards">Guardian Student Media Awards</a></i>, founded in 1999, recognise excellence in journalism and design of British university and college <a href="/wiki/Student_newspapers" class="mw-redirect" title="Student newspapers">student newspapers</a>, magazines and websites.\n</p><p>In memory of <a href="/wiki/Paul_Foot_(journalist)" title="Paul Foot (journalist)">Paul Foot</a>, who died in 2004, <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>Private Eye</i> jointly set up the <a href="/wiki/Paul_Foot_Award" title="Paul Foot Award">Paul Foot Award</a>, with an annual \xc2\xa310,000 prize fund, for investigative or campaigning journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The newspaper also produces <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_100_Best_Footballers_In_The_World" title="The Guardian 100 Best Footballers In The World"><i>The Guardian</i> 100 Best Footballers In The World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_books_lists">Best books lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Best books lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian%27s_100_Best_Novels_Written_in_English" title="The Guardian&#39;s 100 Best Novels Written in English"><i>The Guardian\'</i>s 100 best novels</a> is a list of the best English-language novels as selected by <a href="/wiki/Robert_McCrum" title="Robert McCrum">Robert McCrum</a>.</li>\n<li><i>The Guardian\'</i>s 100 greatest non-fiction book list has come out in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-100_Best_Nonfiction_2011_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100_Best_Nonfiction_2011-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and in 2017, as selected by Robert McCrum.<sup id="cite_ref-100_Best_Nonfiction_2017_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100_Best_Nonfiction_2017-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editors">Editors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> first photographer, July 1908)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eamonn_McCabe" title="Eamonn McCabe">Eamonn McCabe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sean_Smith_(photojournalist_and_filmmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Smith (photojournalist and filmmaker)">Sean Smith</a></li></ul></div>\n<h2><span id="Guardian_News_.26_Media_Archive"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Guardian_News_&amp;_Media_Archive">Guardian News &amp; Media Archive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Guardian News &amp; Media Archive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i>The Guardian</i> and its sister newspaper <i>The Observer</i> opened <i>The Newsroom</i>, an archive and visitor centre in London, in 2002. The centre preserved and promoted the histories and values of the newspapers through its archive, educational programmes and exhibitions. The Newsroom\'s activities were all transferred to <a href="/wiki/Kings_Place" title="Kings Place">Kings Place</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-test_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Now known as the <i>Guardian News &amp; Media Archive</i>, the archive preserves and promotes the histories and values of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i> newspapers by collecting and making accessible material that provides an accurate and comprehensive history of the papers. The archive holds official records of <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i> and also seeks to acquire material from individuals who have been associated with the papers. As well as corporate records, the archive holds correspondence, diaries, notebooks, original cartoons and photographs belonging to staff of the papers.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> This material may be consulted by members of the public by prior appointment. There is also an extensive <i>Manchester Guardian</i> archive at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester" title="University of Manchester">University of Manchester</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands_University_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="John Rylands University Library">John Rylands University Library</a> and there is a collaboration programme between the two archives. The <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a> also has a large archive of <i>The Manchester Guardian</i>, available in online, hard copy, microform, and CD-ROM in their British Library Newspapers collection.\n</p><p>In November 2007 <i>The Guardian</i> and <i>The Observer</i> made their archives available over the internet via DigitalArchive. The current extent of the archives available are 1821 to 2000 for <i>The Guardian</i> and 1791 to 2000 for <i>The Observer</i>: these archives will eventually run up to 2003.\n</p><p>The Newsroom\'s other components were also transferred to Kings Place in 2008. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Education Centre provides a range of educational programmes for students and adults. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> exhibition space was also moved to Kings Place, and has a rolling programme of exhibitions that investigate and reflect upon aspects of news and newspapers and the role of journalism. This programme often draws on the archive collections held in the GNM Archive.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_Monthly" title="Guardian Monthly">Guardian Monthly</a></i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_Weekly" title="The Guardian Weekly">The Guardian Weekly</a></i></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Guardian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.abc.org.uk/product/2451">https://www.abc.org.uk/product/2451</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">The Guardian News and Media Limited (26 July 2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/the-scott-trust/2015/jul/26/the-scott-trust">"The Scott Trust: values and history"</a>. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
